  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8a85e9bd-5db6-452f-b332-976613e8e8ee'
      });

  <span id="freeText3615357041332114750" style="display:none">"How can you love someone so much, and need space from them at the same time?"<br /><br />My alarm goes off at four am. It takes an hour to get to the studio, and then my ballet training begins. I go to school for a few hours, and then it’s back to the studio for more training. Go to bed. Repeat the whole process the next day. <br />I hate it.<br />	My time at school is a blur, except for biology. I don’t rush through that class, because I get to see Roger Byrnes. He probably doesn’t even know I exist, but my heart beats a little faster when I see him walk through the classroom door with his messy hair and carefree attitude. He has so much energy. But then he stares off into the distance, and I wonder what he’s thinking. It’s the highlight of my day. <br />	I wish I could quit ballet so I could be a normal teenager. Someone who Roger would want to be with. I could use some excitement in my life…I bet Roger could give that to me.</span>

<div id="review_2067228181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067228181" />
    <a title="Alkisti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9345673-alkisti"><img alt="Alkisti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470244077p2/9345673.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067228181?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alkisti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alkisti" href="/user/show/9345673-alkisti">Alkisti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067228181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11905911025499073740">** I was a beta reader for this book. **<br/><br/>This was not an easy book to go through, in terms of the themes that it touches but it was an undeniably engrossing one. Lockwood's writing is effortless and was easy to follow. I always found it a difficult task when authors decide to write a book about/for teenagers when they're already adults because it's rare that they get their voices depicted appropriately and realistically. In this case however, the author managed to do a remarkably good job in doin</span>
  <span id="freeText11905911025499073740" style="display:none">** I was a beta reader for this book. **<br /><br />This was not an easy book to go through, in terms of the themes that it touches but it was an undeniably engrossing one. Lockwood's writing is effortless and was easy to follow. I always found it a difficult task when authors decide to write a book about/for teenagers when they're already adults because it's rare that they get their voices depicted appropriately and realistically. In this case however, the author managed to do a remarkably good job in doing that. Nevertheless, there were a few points that appeared a tad on the unrealistic side, too much of a classic "hollywood-teenage-movie" sort of thing. Even though there might have been a bigger reason to justify this, I still found it quite distracting and cheesy sometimes.<br />The main characters, well-developed, vivid and quite intense, can range from being engaging and likeable to obnoxious and suffocating, at least usually not without reasoning.<br />I was actually stressing out through the last chapters, not only because of what they were going through but because the way they scenes and chapters have been written aids to magnify the emotions you get as a reader.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[However, I did miss a confrontation. I could totally relate with Kerri's need to experience<br />life but when Roger dies, she makes it all about her when it shouldn't be. Yes, survivors are the ones experiencing loss, pain, grief etc. and that is by no means an easy thing to do, but there is still a lot of time for her in the future to go through all the grieving stages and the "mystery" of his death but it shouldn't be about her right there and then. Perhaps the important point for the author<br />was to emphasize Roger's illness and where that can lead if not treated or mistreated but I sort of felt like it was an easy way out for Kerri at the same time. She never had to build up the courage and strength to break up with him and take responsibility for her actions and that would have indeed been a brave moment for her, only it never happens. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I think the most important part of this story is that it touches on so many different issues: absent parents, parents living through their children, teenage friendships, alcohol, drugs, having sex for the first time, mental illnesses, death, growing up and the list goes on. It has a lot to tell, especially to teenagers going through similar experiences, so I would recommend it to people around that age group.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11905911025499073740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2129768781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2129768781" />
    <a title="Sara Miller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30941277-sara-miller"><img alt="Sara Miller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446675960p2/30941277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2129768781?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Miller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Miller" href="/user/show/30941277-sara-miller">Sara Miller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2129768781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12029846923038917729">This review will also be posted on Pretty Little Book Blog on Sept 26th as part of the blog tour. <br/><br/>I come from the era when I was a teenager that dance movies were all the rage! (Save The Last Dance, Center Stage, Honey, Step Up. . .) you name it I've seen it! This love of dance gradually transitioned into dance team in high school, Theatre Arts and Dance in college and the love is still there! So when i read the blurb for this book I knew it was one I would love before I had even began the first</span>
  <span id="freeText12029846923038917729" style="display:none">This review will also be posted on Pretty Little Book Blog on Sept 26th as part of the blog tour. <br /><br />I come from the era when I was a teenager that dance movies were all the rage! (Save The Last Dance, Center Stage, Honey, Step Up. . .) you name it I've seen it! This love of dance gradually transitioned into dance team in high school, Theatre Arts and Dance in college and the love is still there! So when i read the blurb for this book I knew it was one I would love before I had even began the first page. It's an incredible thing to feel like you are going to be enthralled by a novel before you even turn the page. . . To feel like the story within the pages can and will change you forever. That the story within the pages can become a small piece of your story (that you can think back years from now and remember exactly what you were wearing and what was going on while you were reading it) this was my whole experience reading All of The Rogers! <br /><br />I loved Kerri's character! She was the best of the best but what do you do when your heart and soul isn't in your craft anymore? Especially when everyone is pushing you into it? Luckily I never had to experience that part but I did go through the having to change what you love due to health reasons. That new beginning stage can be equal parts thrilling and scary as all get out haha. <br /><br />Watching her experience your typical high school things are kind of adorable! And Roger is a HUGE part of this. . . He's a little standoffish at first but we learn that he is dealing with a lot of problems at home, he's a complicated character. Intense and the further we get into the story his behavior begins to take on a different tone. . . Like a lot of young relationships and first loves things are so new and intense you might not notice when things begin to escalate and this story portrays that perfectly! You are going along and things are fun and no nonsense and then all of a sudden there is this conflict and tension, it really snuck up on me! But when we finally find out the reasoning behind all the behaviors Roger is exhibiting this turns into a very brave storyline choice on Erin's part. Not many stories deal with mental health issues teens face in a honest fashion and all of the ups and downs and the struggle just Day to day life takes is portrayed in a truthful manner. <br /><br />This story is a powerful one, if you think it's going to be a cutesy run of the mill YA read, well yes, you have that stuff too but it's more than that! It's first love, heartache, learning about yourself and what you need, it's about self respect and family, and learning that it's okay to challenge things and ideas and it's okay to cry. So many different themes are wrapped up in here so I'm just going to leave you with this. Read it, talk about it, and remove the stigma from mental health issues. Be a part of the conversation and not a part of sweeping it under the rug. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12029846923038917729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2071813846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6203385781956610499">All the Rogers- enjoyable read with unexpected twists. This book transported me back to being a young adult where I felt like I was living right along with the characters. Character development was on point- the descriptions of both the characters and the scenes was detailed enough without being too detailed. <br/>I was a Beta reader and read a pre-release copy.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2074671887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2074671887" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10787335-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505591187p2/10787335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2074671887?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/10787335-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2074671887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9396939076747854952">I'm coming to understand that Erin Lockwood's magic is some kind of alchemical combination that produces novels that I always walk away from feeling like "that was just right." Consistently pulling off just right is no simple feat. First one must be a storyteller. You have to have intuitions about how the human mind consumes and digests narrative and then be able to translate those instincts into a story. All of the Rogers is Lockwood's best storytelling to date, and she proves herself to have t</span>
  <span id="freeText9396939076747854952" style="display:none">I'm coming to understand that Erin Lockwood's magic is some kind of alchemical combination that produces novels that I always walk away from feeling like "that was just right." Consistently pulling off just right is no simple feat. First one must be a storyteller. You have to have intuitions about how the human mind consumes and digests narrative and then be able to translate those instincts into a story. All of the Rogers is Lockwood's best storytelling to date, and she proves herself to have those instincts in spades. Plot development happens in a way that feels extremely realistic and concurrently enchanted. The unfolding of a teen summer romance is described in a way that captures something that many of us have forgotten as adults. We hold onto specific memories, but cannot reconnect to the lived experience of what it was like when we ventured into the intoxicating and sublime world of romantic love for the very first time. All of the Rogers description of this feels somewhat like remembering a forgotten dream, and is an absolute treat to read. But the book is just right, and that means that with impressive subtlety and nuance Lockwood guides readers through the process of waking up, which is an inevitability that we rarely realize while dreaming. Do you remember what it was like when it dawned on you that love was much more complex than the initial whirlwind? First loves are absolutely nothing if not fertile ground for a whole host of learning experiences. All of the Rogers describes the confusing, painful, and essentially messy nature of that learning process. I loved the ambivalence of the protagonist and the struggle to understand what exactly was happening and what to do with that information. It's a highly relatable experience that was laid out in a way that felt...yeah, just right. Thematically the book goes on to grapple with mental health issues in young people and the implications of the haphazard quest to mitigate their effects. All of the Rogers dives into waters of our human reality that run very deep. The bottom of those depths are not penetrated by sunlight and are populated with all manner of monsters. Lockwood takes us on a guided exploration of those waters where there is plenty of sunlight and we can look around without any fear of being eaten. That is, she manages to creatively approach a very challenging topic with sensitivity and honesty, but without being excessively distressing. We're not headed to the terrifying depths, but we're definitely jumping in, and that's what good YA literature should do, I think. It's a moving book that won't wreck you. It's a fun book that will challenge you a bit. At its core it's an highly enjoyable read that offered some legitimately insightful commentary without ever feeling inaccessible or difficult to swallow. It was interesting. It was well executed. It was balanced. It was, you know, just right.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9396939076747854952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2126104669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126104669" />
    <a title="Paula  Phillips" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1969584-paula-phillips"><img alt="Paula  Phillips" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574564336p2/1969584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126104669?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula  Phillips" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula  Phillips" href="/user/show/1969584-paula-phillips">Paula  Phillips</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126104669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9248945969559519125">For most of Kerri's life, she has been dedicated to dancing and becoming the best and becoming what her Mother wanted to be but missed out on the opportunity. The thing is Kerri doesn't want to be a dancer and injures herself on purpose to stuff up her audition for Julliard. The plan works, and for her senior year, Kerri has a chance to become a normal teenager. With the help of her best friends, she starts to do everything a rebellious teenager does like heading to parties and hooking up with b</span>
  <span id="freeText9248945969559519125" style="display:none">For most of Kerri's life, she has been dedicated to dancing and becoming the best and becoming what her Mother wanted to be but missed out on the opportunity. The thing is Kerri doesn't want to be a dancer and injures herself on purpose to stuff up her audition for Julliard. The plan works, and for her senior year, Kerri has a chance to become a normal teenager. With the help of her best friends, she starts to do everything a rebellious teenager does like heading to parties and hooking up with boys - one in particular Roger. Roger has been Kerri's crush for a while now, and the pair starts dating. Thing is though that Roger has some home and personal problems and the relationship starts to become unbalanced. During the book, we can see that Roger heavily relies on Kerri to make him happy. Kerri is getting ready to go to college, and every time she tries to break up with Roger, she finds herself sucked back into his life. What will happen when Kerri heads off to college and finds herself meeting new people, and she discovers she no longer needs Roger? How will Roger take the news? This book does touch on some edgy issues and features mental health and suicide. After reading this, it did get me thinking as this week featured World Suicide Day on the 10th September. It also gives readers the thought of how far would you go to save someone before you find yourself being pulled down too? All of the Rogers is a coming of age story that touches everyone who has ever had a family or romantic co-dependent relationship.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9248945969559519125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Bryant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Bryant" href="/user/show/19344998-tara-bryant">Tara Bryant</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer10949789873285359183">All Of The Rogers<br/>By Erin Lockwood<br/><br/>I had the honour of reading and reviewing All Of The Rogers, a novel by Erin Lockwood. <br/><br/>This book did me in! The emotions I had while reading All Of The Rogers had me feeling like I was on an emotional roller coaster. The ups, downs, happy, sad, worried and broken. Taking us back to high school, the setting Erin portrays takes us into real life struggles that teenagers deal with everyday. The relationships with peers, parents and teachers, as well as the drama tha</span>
  <span id="freeText10949789873285359183" style="display:none">All Of The Rogers<br />By Erin Lockwood<br /><br />I had the honour of reading and reviewing All Of The Rogers, a novel by Erin Lockwood. <br /><br />This book did me in! The emotions I had while reading All Of The Rogers had me feeling like I was on an emotional roller coaster. The ups, downs, happy, sad, worried and broken. Taking us back to high school, the setting Erin portrays takes us into real life struggles that teenagers deal with everyday. The relationships with peers, parents and teachers, as well as the drama that comes with each of these topics. <br /><br />"I want to be a normal teenager. I just have no idea how. This isn’t going to be easy. But, for the first time in a long time, I’m excited about my future."<br /><br />One of the topics most prevalent in All Of The Rogers is mental illness. The reality of how hard it is for people to talk about it and how it isn't so easily diagnosed, made this book all the more real. Erin touched on topics most people wouldn't dare talk about, and to me, this book will help others feel that it is ok to talk about mental illness. <br /><br />"I look into his eyes, half-begging him to kiss me and half-telling him to stop cutting off communication when he’s upset. That means he will have to talk to me when he’s mad, instead of falling off the face of the earth and then pretending like nothing ever happened when he comes back up."<br /><br />The characters in All Of The Rogers are so relatable, from the awkward wall flower, to the cutest boy with the secrets, to the popular girl that will do anything for attention, Erin's descriptive writing helps us connect with each character on different levels. <br /><br />"If anyone applauds, I don’t hear it. All I hear is a ringing in my ears. Suddenly, I can feel the effects of not eating or drinking all day. Instead of going back to my seat, I move to the side and push through the doors, stumbling into the hallway. My back slides against the wall, and I hug my knees, hanging my head and crying."<br /><br />I came into reading All Of The Rogers with a completely open mind, and within the first 20 pages I was hooked. As I kept reading each word tugged at my heart strings and gave me all the feels. By the end I was a mess of tears. All The Rogers is now in my top 5 favourite books!<br /><br />⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Tara</span>

<div id="review_2088659019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088659019" />
    <a title="Steve Elbe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40062248-steve-elbe"><img alt="Steve Elbe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423402120p2/40062248.jpg" /></a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2088659019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2853763723993581313">This is my 3rd Lockwood book I've had the privilege to read prior to release and it once again does not disappoint. All 3 novels have romance but are all different, I wonder where she will go next, suspense is always another common denominator. I refuse to give anything away but strongly recommend you give this story a read.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081274477" />
    <a title="Sara Blanchard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98118-sara-blanchard"><img alt="Sara Blanchard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540575222p2/98118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9146721249623926998">I was an enthralled beta reader, devouring this book and even shouting out loud at a particularly shocking scene. All of the Rogers is a heavier read than I had come to expect of the author. In it, Erin Lockwood weaves a masterful tale, one that eases you into a typical teenage relationship that reveals itself to be so much more. Thought-provoking, emotional and with a dramatic punch, All of the Rogers makes you question how you perceive people and what love really means.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42609491-lauren?shelf=2018-books-read">2018-books-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2266515567" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16469068517822239746">I did not think that this book would be as intense as it was. I didn’t think I’d stay up till 1:30 in the morning in tears finishing it either. This is a great read for anyone but I think especially young adults. It discusses the concepts of healthy vs non healthy relationships whether that be or the friend or romantic variety. It also discusses mental illness, independence, dependency (of different varieties as well), commitment and other concepts that you may face that are hard to discuss. Wha</span>
  <span id="freeText16469068517822239746" style="display:none">I did not think that this book would be as intense as it was. I didn’t think I’d stay up till 1:30 in the morning in tears finishing it either. This is a great read for anyone but I think especially young adults. It discusses the concepts of healthy vs non healthy relationships whether that be or the friend or romantic variety. It also discusses mental illness, independence, dependency (of different varieties as well), commitment and other concepts that you may face that are hard to discuss. What’s stopping me from giving this a 5 star rating is that I didn’t fully love the book. I think the Author did a great job and I did stay up all night finishing it so I undoubtedly really liked the book but something was missing for me. I think this is a great read and I would highly recommend it to others and maybe to any English teacher friends looking for YA book clubs for students (there is some adult content though). </span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ages 16+</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7863634-lynda-dickson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2205897975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11576550834732919092">After dedicating her whole life to ballet, Kerri has finally had enough. She deliberately injures herself to tank an audition for Juilliard and settles in for her final year of high school as a "normal" teenager. First on her agenda is attending a party, second is talking to her crush Roger. <br/><br/>I couldn't tell if Roger was super-nice or a creep in disguise, but reason for his fluctuating behavior becomes apparent as the book progresses, hence the title. Kerri's mother is heartbreakingly uncaring an</span>
  <span id="freeText11576550834732919092" style="display:none">After dedicating her whole life to ballet, Kerri has finally had enough. She deliberately injures herself to tank an audition for Juilliard and settles in for her final year of high school as a "normal" teenager. First on her agenda is attending a party, second is talking to her crush Roger. <br /><br />I couldn't tell if Roger was super-nice or a creep in disguise, but reason for his fluctuating behavior becomes apparent as the book progresses, hence the title. Kerri's mother is heartbreakingly uncaring and Roger's mother is even more useless. At least Kerri has her brother Bradley - he's the best. And Roger and Kerri have his godmother Diane.<br /><br />Through the narrative, the author provides a lot of thinly veiled advice for teenagers on such pertinent topics as drink driving, sex, contraception, mental illness, and death.<br /><br />Warnings: underage drinking, coarse language, sex scenes (not graphic), mental health.<br /><br />I received this book in return for an honest review.<br /><br />Full blog post: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://booksdirectonline.blogspot.com/2017/12/all-of-the-rogers-by-erin-lockwood.html">https://booksdirectonline.blogspot.co...</a></span>

    <a title="Kaitlyn Joy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23541650-kaitlyn-joy"><img alt="Kaitlyn Joy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377917061p2/23541650.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2476809321?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlyn Joy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlyn Joy" href="/user/show/23541650-kaitlyn-joy">Kaitlyn Joy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23541650-kaitlyn-joy?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23541650-kaitlyn-joy?shelf=kindle-unlimited">kindle-unlimited</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2476809321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13512463084906431366">This book isn't a hard book, I actually read it in a day and it was in the midst of doing other things. This book handles a question of mental illness in young adults, the challenge of a diagnosis, and the impact on the lives of people we love. <br/><br/>Kerri, is a former ballerina, she never wanted to be a ballerina, but it was her mother's dream, and now that she's blown her Juliard audition, things are tense with her mother. The story starts off as Kerri's tries to adapt to life as a normal teenager a</span>
  <span id="freeText13512463084906431366" style="display:none">This book isn't a hard book, I actually read it in a day and it was in the midst of doing other things. This book handles a question of mental illness in young adults, the challenge of a diagnosis, and the impact on the lives of people we love. <br /><br />Kerri, is a former ballerina, she never wanted to be a ballerina, but it was her mother's dream, and now that she's blown her Juliard audition, things are tense with her mother. The story starts off as Kerri's tries to adapt to life as a normal teenager and almost immediately falls in with Roger. Roger is enthusiastic and emotive and his personality just makes people around him happy. They begin to fall in love but as Kerri and Roger fall in love, another side of Roger appears the one that is overly emotional and intense. This book continues while we watch Roger's highs and lows. <br /><br />The book handles a difficult topic and could have been handled poorly, but the fact that the author made Kerri in touch with the fact that Roger was going through bipolar disorder and recognizing this emotive behavior and being concerned about him while also knowing that she didn't deserve to be treated poorly, made both characters redeeming. I'd recommend, it's a quick but emotional read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13512463084906431366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2182486822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5581143737233384520">Heartwarming and Gutwrenching, 'All of the Rogers' was an emotional coin, flipping constantly from one happy extreme to the worst. Lockwood did an amazing job writing this story! Everything was, I felt, in fluid perfection from the toxic characters, the mentally sound influencers, the plot- it came together so wonderfully. If this was a movie, I'd watch it every bittersweet moment. (Thinking along the lines of 'The Fault in Our Stars'.) In the beginning, I expected it to be a 'coming into your o</span>
  <span id="freeText5581143737233384520" style="display:none">Heartwarming and Gutwrenching, 'All of the Rogers' was an emotional coin, flipping constantly from one happy extreme to the worst. Lockwood did an amazing job writing this story! Everything was, I felt, in fluid perfection from the toxic characters, the mentally sound influencers, the plot- it came together so wonderfully. If this was a movie, I'd watch it every bittersweet moment. (Thinking along the lines of 'The Fault in Our Stars'.) In the beginning, I expected it to be a 'coming into your own' type of story. However, the deeper emotional, mature issues underlying Roger and Kerri's intense, loving, clingy relationship progressed the story into something more. An insight as to these types of relationships with someone who has an undetermined mental illness. It was a great book. One that'll stick with me for a while. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5581143737233384520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2362381723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17586639656740883720"><strong>Page turner! </strong><br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book and kept wondering what was coming next! The author did a great job of making you feel so many emotions for her characters. I think the subject matter is important and not talked about a lot. Mental health issues are not well understood by many and the struggles they Kerri went through (though of course harder given the circumstances) are pressures many teenagers go through and very relatable. This book was very well written and I would definitely recommen</span>
  <span id="freeText17586639656740883720" style="display:none"><strong>Page turner! </strong><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and kept wondering what was coming next! The author did a great job of making you feel so many emotions for her characters. I think the subject matter is important and not talked about a lot. Mental health issues are not well understood by many and the struggles they Kerri went through (though of course harder given the circumstances) are pressures many teenagers go through and very relatable. This book was very well written and I would definitely recommend it! </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_42745424'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42745424-that-boy"><img alt="That Boy (That Boy, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1541865239l/42745424._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Awd1eHGXKZjSKBItPD4llUImQ+LXMrEH3p4maHD5TfIUoxmjMH/VlbIlASYGdXulivledQY9o9A3OCYeLKK3RA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WH9KTB2sZP8+5eb3pC8F5Y100hXfhRIbpPP2YSU3jHlP2yaXXESY8l7o9fyeZFvVRavPgg6KAMxNVfYXeWx2zw==')})
  }

</script>

  //]]>
</script>
